Shade in | Make a part of a picture darker | She SHADED IN the area under the tree. | true
Shade out | Leave a place without saying goodbye | The party was so dull that I decided to SHADE OUT. | false
Light out | Leave suddenly | When Zeke found out they were coming for him he LIT OUT for the border. | false
Light up | Light or start smoking a cigarette | Asif LIT UP as soon as he got out of the building. | true
Light up | Illuminate | They LIGHT UP the streets at Christmas time. | true
Smoke out | Force someone out of a place they're hiding in | The police SMOKED the gang OUT and arrested them. | true
Venture forth | Leave somewhere safe or comfortable | If the storm has finished, we could VENTURE FORTH. | false
Fawn on | Praise someone in an excessive way to get their favour or something from them | He's always FAWNING ON his boss to try to get promoted. | false
Fawn over | Praise someone in an excessive way to get their favour or something from them | She FAWNED OVER the inspectors in the hope that they would give her a good grade. | false
Trip out | Be under the influence of psychoactive drugs | After taking the LSD he TRIPPED OUT for hours. | false
Trip over | Fall | I TRIPPED OVER and hurt my knee. | false
Trip over | Fall because you hit an obstacle | I TRIPPED OVER the kerb and broke my nose. | false
Trip up | Make a mistake | I TRIPPED UP in the interview when they asked me about what I could offer the company. | false
Bargain down | Persuade someone to drop the price of something they're selling | I BARGAINED her DOWN to half what she originally wanted. | true
Bargain for | Expect something to happen (usually negative) | I hadn't BARGAINED FOR so many people coming. | false
Bargain on | Expect something to happen (usually negative) | I hadn't BARGAINED ON him coming. | false
Suit up | Get dressed or put on a uniform for an activity or task | They SUITED UP and went to the interview | false
Suit up | Wear a condom | You should always SUIT UP when having sex with someone you don't know. | false
Jog along | Make progress or move ahead, but not very fast | Works JOGGING ALONG- nothing special. | false
Jog on | Go away | JOG ON and leave me alone. | false
Zip around | Move quickly | We ZIPPED AROUND the supermarket to get the shopping done. | false
Zip by | Pass quickly | The motorbike ZIPPED BY the cars stuck in the traffic jam. | false
Zip it | Keep quiet, say nothing | He told me to ZIP IT, so I said nothing. | false
Zip up | Keep quiet | He was being stupid in the meeting, so we told him to ZIP UP. | false
Embark on | Start a project or venture | Piere EMBARKED ON an MBA at Insead last autumn. | false
Embark upon | Start a project or venture | Fernanda has just EMBARKED UPON a new professional challenge. | false
Rip off | Charge excessively or obtain money unfairly | Tourists get RIPPED OFF a lot when they don't speak the language. | true
Rip on | Criticise or insult | The media are RIPPING ON the government. | false
Tighten up | Make something more secure or function better | They're TIGHTENING UP security for the president's visit. | true

Cast around for | Try to find something | She was CASTING AROUND FOR people to help her. | false

Cast off | Dispose, get rid of | They CAST OFF any semblance of politeness and attacked us viciously. | true
Cast off | Untie a boat so it's free to sail | They CAST OFF and headed out to sea. | false
Cast out | Expel, reject | They CAST him OUT because of his behaviour. | true
Cast round for | Try to find something | He CAST ROUND FOR any sign of his things. | false
Cast up | Be left on the shore by the sea | The rubbish was CAST UP by the tide. | true

Work out | End nicely | Things were going wrong for them but fortunately it all WORKED OUT in the end. | false

Work over | Examine carefully | They WORKED OVER the market looking for bargains. | true
Work through | Deal with, resolve a problem, often emotional | It took him a long time to WORK THROUGH his anger after he lost his job. | false

Pig off | Used to tell someone to get lost or leave you alone | He told them to PIG OFF and leave him in peace. | false
Pig out | Eat a lot | The food was great, so I really PIGGED OUT. | false
Hanker after | Want something a lot, especially if you shouldn't want it or can't have it | I'm supposed to be on a diet and I can't stop HANKERING AFTER some chocolate. | false
Hanker for | Want something a lot, especially if you shouldn't want it or can't have it | I have always HANKERED FOR a soft-top car. | false
